$(window).load(function(){
	if ($('#user_login_control').is(':empty')){
	$.ajax({
		url: "http://reason.com/ajax/commenthandle",
		dataType: 'json',
		success: function(data) {
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
			$(document).trigger('adminview',[data]);
		},
		error: function(xhr, textStatus){
			var data = { logged_in:null, error:textStatus };
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
		}
	});

	$('.commentsheading &gt; span &gt; a').click(function(){
		document.location.hash = 'comment';
	});
	}
});


$(document).ready(function(){
	$.ajax({
		url: "http://reason.com/ajax/commenthandle",
		dataType: 'json',
		success: function(data) {
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
			$(document).trigger('adminview',[data]);
		},
		error: function(xhr, textStatus){
			var data = { logged_in:null, error:textStatus };
			$(document).trigger('loginStatus', [data]);
		}
	});

	$('.commentsheading &gt; span &gt; a').click(function(){
		document.location.hash = 'comment';
	});

	if (window.location.hash.match(/^#comment/)) {
			var cctrl = $('.commentcontrol'), cctnr = $('#commentcontainer');
			cctrl.addClass('open');
			cctnr.show();
			$('#commentform.cancomment').show();
		
	}else{
			var cctrl = $('.commentcontrol'), cctnr = $('#commentcontainer');
			cctnr.hide();
			cctrl.removeClass('open');
			cctrl.one('click', function(e) {
				cctrl.addClass('open');
				cctnr.show();
				$('#commentform.cancomment').show();
			});
	}
	if($.cookie('fontSize')) {
		var fontSize = $.cookie('fontSize');
 		$('article.post').css({'font-size':fontSize});
 		$('ul.posts').css({'font-size':fontSize});
 	}

	// SIDR PANELS

	$('#mobile-nav-toggle').unbind('onclick');
	$('#mobile-nav-toggle').sidr({
		displace: false,
		name: 'sidr-main',
		source: '#site-navigation',
		side:'right'
	});
	jQuery('#sidr-main .sidr-class-closemenu a').click(function(){
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
		jQuery('.small-share').show();
	});
	jQuery('.container_24').click(function(){
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
	});
	jQuery('#mobile-nav-toggle').click(function(){
		jQuery('.small-share').hide();
	});


	$('#mobile-trending-toggle').unbind('onclick');
	jQuery('#mobile-trending-toggle').sidr({
		displace: false,
		name: 'sidr-trending',
		source: '#trending-navigation',
		side: 'left'
	});
	jQuery('#sidr-trending .sidr-class-closemenu a').click(function(){

        jQuery('.small-share').show();
	});
	jQuery('.container_24').click(function(){
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-trending');
	});
	jQuery('#mobile-trending-toggle').click(function(){
		jQuery('.small-share').hide();
	});
	jQuery(window).resize(function () {
		if (jQuery(window).width() &gt; 700) {
			jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
			jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-trending');
		}
	});

	// let's do this in jquery so we're sure it's stacked
	$('textarea').focus( function() {
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-main');
		jQuery.sidr('close', 'sidr-trending');
	});
	// $.sidr('open', 'sidr-main');

	function setScaleable(x) {
		originalval = $('head meta[name=viewport]').attr('content');
		newval = originalval.replace(/(user-scalable=)\d{1,9}/g, '$1'+x);
		if (originalval.localeCompare(newval)) {
			$('head meta[name=viewport]').attr('content', newval);
		} else {
			$('head meta[name=viewport]').attr('content', originalval+', user-scalable='+x);
		}
	}

	//we don't want the screen to scale up when we select a text item, so we're going to prevent it by turning it on and off as we enter and leave
	$('textarea, input').on('focusin', function() {
		setScaleable(0);
	});

	$('textaream, input').on('focusout', function() {
		setScaleable(1);
	});

	// there's some visual element eh when people leave the screen, possibly because of fixed position
	// and element destruction order. We're going to simply hide these items on the way out to make sure
	// they don't jump around
	$( window ).unload(function() {
  		$('#nav1').hide();
  		$('#sidr-main').hide();
  		$('#sidr-trending').hide();
	});


	$("a#sidr-id-fontbigger").click(function() {
 		$('ul.posts').css('font-size', function(index,value) {
 			var fontSize = parseInt(value) + 1 + 'px';
	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });
	 		return fontSize;
 		});
 		$('#right-col').css('font-size', function(index,value) {
 			var fontSize = parseInt(value) + 1 + 'px';
	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });
	 		return fontSize;
 		});
  		$('article.post').css('font-size', function(index,value) {
 			var fontSize = parseInt(value) + 1 + 'px';
	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });
	 		return fontSize;
 		});
	});

	$("a#sidr-id-fontsmaller").click(function() {
 		$('ul.posts').css('font-size', function(index,value) {
 			var fontSize = parseInt(value) - 1 + 'px';
	 		$.cookie('fontSize',fontSize, { path: '/', expires: 7 });

window.USERSTATE = {logged_in:null};
$(document).bind('loginStatus', function(e, d) {
	$.extend(window.USERSTATE, d);
});

	$(document).bind('adminview', function(e, d) {
		if(d.isadmin){
			$("body").addClass("adminlogin");
			window.ADMININFO = JSONObject= {
				"baseurl":"http://reason.com/",
				"showeditbutton":1,
				"showadminbar":1,
				"showcommentcontrols":1,
				"usersettingsurl":"http://reason.com/admin/users//modify",
				"commentactions" : 0};
			$.getScript("/media/js/navtools.js");
		}
	});

function updateCountdowns() {
	editbuttons = $('button.comment_edit:visible');
	if (editbuttons.length) {
		editbuttons.each(function() {
			timeremaining = $(this).data('editwindow-remaining');
			if (--timeremaining &lt; 0) {
				$(this).text('edit timer expired');
				$(this).fadeOut(); //no need for further time update; we only poll visibles
			} else {
				$(this).text('edit ('+timeremaining+' seconds remaining)');
				$(this).data('editwindow-remaining', timeremaining);
			}
		})
	} else {
		//no reason to keep this running when there's nothing to update
		clearInterval(countdownTimer);
	}
}

var countdownTimer = null;

$(document).bind('loginStatus', function(e,d){
	servertime = Number(d.unixtime);
	editing_window_seconds = Number(d.editing_window_seconds);
	if (d.logged_in) {
		userID = d.user_id;
		var handle = $("#user_login_control")
		.html('&lt;p&gt;You are currently logged in as: &lt;strong&gt;&lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/manage" class="handle"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/strong&gt;. &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/logout"&gt;&lt;span&gt;Sign Out&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;/p&gt;')
		.find('.handle')
		handle.text(d.handle)
		handle.attr('href', handle.attr('href')+'/'+userID);
		//look for all the editable comments by this user
		$('div#commentcontainer li[data-user-id='+userID+']').each(function( index ) {
			commenttimestamp = Number($(this).data('comment-timestamp'));
			elapsedtime = servertime - commenttimestamp;
			if (elapsedtime &lt; editing_window_seconds) {
				secondsremaining = editing_window_seconds - elapsedtime;
				$(this).find('button.comment_edit').show().data('editwindow-remaining', secondsremaining);
			}
		});
		countdownTimer = setInterval(updateCountdowns, 1E3);
	} else {
		$("#user_login_control").html('&lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/login"&gt;&lt;span&gt;Login&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt; or &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/register"&gt;&lt;span&gt;Sign-up&lt;/span&gt;&lt;/a&gt;');
	}
});

(function(){
	var threadedCommentRepliesActive=null;
	var cb = $('#commentcontainer');

	function cmtLoginStatusHandler(e,d) {
		var lc = $('#commentform'), clr = $('.comment_login_require');
		if (d.logged_in) {
			clr.hide();
			lc.addClass('cancomment');
			lc.find('.logged_in_as').remove();
			var handle = lc.children('form')
			.prepend('&lt;div class="logged_in_as"&gt;&lt;p&gt;You are currently logged in as &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/manage/'+d.user_id+'" class="handle"&gt;&lt;/a&gt;. Not you? &lt;a href="http://reason.com/users/logout"&gt;Sign out&lt;/a&gt;.&lt;/p&gt;&lt;/div&gt;')
			.find('.handle');
			handle.text(d.handle);
			handle.attr('a', handle.attr('a')+'/'+d.user_id);
			lc.show();
			threadedCommentReplies(true);
			editComments(true);
		} else if (d.logged_in===false) {
			clr.show();
			lc.removeClass('cancomment');
			threadedCommentReplies(false);
		} else {
			clr.html('&lt;p&gt;Oops, something went wrong and we can\'t tell if you\'re logged in. Please referesh and try again.&lt;/p&gt;');
		}
	}

	function threadedCommentReplies(activate){
		var cb = $('#commentcontainer');
		if (activate) {
			cb.find('.comment_reply').show();
			cb.find('.comment_reply_msg').hide();
			if (!threadedCommentRepliesActive &amp;&amp; (typeof(CommentReplyForm) !== "undefined")) {
				var template = CommentReplyForm.preparetemplate('commentform');
				var crf = new CommentReplyForm(template);
				crf.bindHandlers('li.com-block button.comment_reply');
				var previewurl = $('#commentform form').attr('action').replace(/\/post$/, '/preview');
				CommentPreview.bindHandlers(template, template.find(':button.preview'), previewurl);
				CommentPreview.bindHandlers($('#commentform'), $('#commentform :button.preview'), previewurl);
			}
		} else {
			cb.find('.comment_reply').hide();
			cb.find('.comment_reply_msg').show();
			cb.find('.leave-comment').hide();
		}
	}

	function editComments(activate) {
		var cb = $('#commentcontainer');
		if (activate) {
			//we find only the ones made visible during initialization; no reason to bind the rest.
			// active_edit_buttons = $('button.comment_edit:visible');
			if (typeof(CommentEditForm) !== "undefined") {
				var template = CommentEditForm.preparetemplate('commenteditform');
				var crf = new CommentEditForm(template);
				crf.bindHandlers('button.comment_edit:visible');
			}
		} else {
			cb.find('button.comment_edit').hide();
		}
	}
	$(document).bind('loginStatus', cmtLoginStatusHandler);


})();

								$(function () {

											$('#clicktospritz_125786').toggle();
										}
										function spritz_125786init() {
										    var onSpritzifySuccess = function(spritzText) {
												console.log('Spritzify success');
										        spritzController.startSpritzing(spritzText);
										    };
										    var onSpritzifyError = function(error) {
										        alert("Unable to Spritz: " + error.message);
										    };

											var customOptions = {
											        placeholderText:    { startText: 'Nope' },
											        header: 			{	login: false,
											        						close: true,
											        						closeHandler: spritz_125786_visibility },

												// Attach the controller's container to this page's "spritzer" container
												spritzController.attach($('#spritzer_125786'));
										    }										    // this would be the most basic and inclusive way, but we really want to avoid reading photo captions etc
										    // text = $('#spritzer_125786').parents('article').find('div.postcontent').text();
										    var text = '';
										    var textNodes = $('#spritzer_125786').parents('article').find('div.postcontent').find('p');

										    // we want to exclude spans since they're how our image captions are enclosed
										    for (var i = 0; i &lt; textNodes.length; i++) {
												text += $(textNodes[i])
												    .clone()    //clone the element
												    .children() //select all the children
												    .remove('span')   //remove all the children
												    .end()  //again go back to selected element
												    .text() + '\n\n';
										        // text += $(textNodes[i]).text() + '\n\n';
										    }
											var locale = "en_us;";
										    // Send to SpritzEngine to translate
										    SpritzClient.spritzify(text, locale, onSpritzifySuccess, onSpritzifyError);
										}

										$(document).on('spritz_loaded', function() {
											console.log('Spritz loaded');
										   // Code that depends on a an initialized SpritzClient goes here
											spritz_125786_visibility();
											spritz_125786init();


										}); //end spritz_loaded

										if (typeof SpritzClient === 'undefined') {
											$.getScript('//sdk.spritzinc.com/js/1.2/js/spritz.min.js', function() {
												console.log('Spritz.min.js loaded');
											});
										} else {
											spritz_125786_visibility();
											spritz_125786init();
										}
									};
									$('#clicktospritz_125786').click(function() {spritz_125786(); return false;});
								})
            </script>
           </li>
           <li class="clear">
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
        </aside>
        <div class="clear">
        </div>
        <div class="audio" style="display:none;">
        </div>
       </header>
       <!--&lt;div class='google-ad'&gt;-->
       <!--&lt;/div&gt;-->
       <div class="p402_premium">
        <div class="entry postcontent">
         <p>
          There are two kinds of people in the world: the kind who think
it's perfectly reasonable to strip-search a 13-year-old girl
suspected of bringing ibuprofen to school, and the kind who think
those people should be kept as far away from children as possible.
The first group includes officials at Safford Middle School in
Safford, Arizona, who in 2003 forced eighth-grader Savana Redding
to prove she was not concealing Advil in her crotch or
cleavage.
         </p>
         <section class="asidecontainer p402_hide desktop-only">
          <aside class="relatedinfo">
           <section class="relatedarticles">
            <header>
             <h3>
              RELATED ARTICLES
             </h3>
            </header>

               </time>
              </p>
             </li>

               </a>

               </a>
               <span class="pipe">

               </span>

                6.23.15
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>

               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">

               </a>
               <span class="pipe">

               </time>

           <section class="morearticles">
            <h3>
             MORE ARTICLES BY
             <a href="http://reason.com/people/jacob-sullum/all">
              Jacob Sullum
             </a>
            </h3>
            <ul>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/archives/2015/07/08/christie-vs-paul-on-surveillance-and-sec">
                Christie vs. Paul on Surveillance and Security
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <time datetime="2015-07-08T11:00:00+00:00">
                7.08.15 7:00 am
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/archives/2015/07/05/how-libertarian-is-rand-paul-on-marijuan">
                How Libertarian Is Rand Paul on Drug Policy?
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <time datetime="2015-07-05T12:30:00+00:00">
                7.05.15 8:30 am
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
             <li>
              <h4>
               <a href="http://reason.com/archives/2015/07/01/which-states-will-legalize-pot">
                Which States Will Legalize Pot Next?
               </a>
              </h4>
              <p class="meta">
               <time datetime="2015-07-01T16:00:00+00:00">
                7.01.15 12:00 pm
               </time>
              </p>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </section>
           <section class="relatedtopics">
            <ul>
             <li>
              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/drug-policy">
               Drug Policy
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/privacy">
               Privacy
              </a>
             </li>
             <li>
              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/education">
               Education
              </a>
             </li>

              <a href="http://reason.com/tags/constitutional-law">
               Constitutional Law
              </a>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </section>
          </aside>
         </section>
         <p>
          It also includes two judges on the U.S. Court of Appeals for the
9th Circuit, who last fall
          <a href="http://caselaw.lp.findlaw.com/data2/circs/9th/0515759p.pdf">
           ruled
          </a>
          that the strip search did not violate Savana's Fourth Amendment
rights. The full court, which recently
          <a href="http://www.azstarnet.com/sn/hourlyupdate/231628.php">
           heard
          </a>
          oral arguments in the case, now has an opportunity to overturn that
decision and vote against a legal environment in which
schoolchildren are conditioned to believe government agents have
the authority to subject people to invasive, humiliating searches
on the slightest pretext.
         </p>
         <p>
          Safford Middle School has a "zero tolerance" policy that
prohibits possession of all drugs, including not just alcohol and
illegal intoxicants but prescription medications and
over-the-counter remedies, "except those for which permission to
use in school has been granted." In October 2003, acting on a tip,
Vice Principal Kerry Wilson found a few 400-milligram ibuprofen
pills (each equivalent to two over-the-counter tablets) and one
nonprescription naproxen tablet in the pockets of a student named
Marissa, who claimed Savana was her source.
         </p>
         <p>
          Savana, an honors student with no history of disciplinary
trouble or drug problems, said she didn't know anything about the
pills and agreed to a search of her backpack, which turned up
nothing incriminating. Wilson nevertheless instructed a female
secretary to strip-search Savana under the school nurse's
supervision, without even bothering to contact the girl's
mother.
         </p>
         <p>
          The secretary had Savana take off all her clothing except her
underwear. Then she told her to "pull her bra out and to the side
and shake it, exposing her breasts," and "pull her underwear out at
the crotch and shake it, exposing her pelvic area." Sometimes it's
hard to tell the difference between drug warriors and child
molesters.
         </p>
         <p>
          "I was embarrassed and scared," Savana
          <a href="http://72.3.233.244/drugpolicy/search/34293lgl20041103.html">
           said
          </a>
          in an affidavit, "but felt I would be in more trouble if I did not
do what they asked. I held my head down so they could not see I was
about to cry." She called it "the most humiliating experience I
have ever had." Later, she recalled, the principal, Robert Beeman,
said "he did not think the strip search was a big deal because they
did not find anything."
         </p>
         <div class="ym" id="ym_1044036704457308825">
         </div>
         <script type="text/javascript">
          (function(e,t){if(t._ym===void 0){t._ym="";var m=e.createElement("script");m.type="text/javascript",m.async=!0,m.src="//static.yieldmo.com/ym.m5.js",(e.getElementsByTagName("head")[0]||e.getElementsByTagName("body")[0]).appendChild(m)}else t._ym instanceof String||void 0===t._ym.chkPls||t._ym.chkPls()})(document,window);
         </script>
         <p>
          The U.S. Supreme Court has
          <a href="http://caselaw.lp.findlaw.com/scripts/getcase.pl?navby=case&amp;court=us&amp;vol=469&amp;page=325">
           held
          </a>
          that a public school official's search of a student is
constitutional if it is "justified at its inception" and
"reasonably related in scope to the circumstances which justified
the interference in the first place." This search was neither.
         </p>
         <p>
          When Wilson ordered the search, the only evidence that Savana
had violated school policy was the uncorroborated accusation from
Marissa, who was in trouble herself and eager to shift the blame.
Even Marissa (who had pills in her pockets, not her underwear) did
not claim that Savana currently possessed any pills, let alone that
she had hidden them under her clothes.
         </p>
         <p>
          Savana, who was closely supervised after Wilson approached her,
did not have an opportunity to stash contraband. As the American
Civil Liberties Union
          <a href="http://72.3.233.244/drugpolicy/search/34289lgl20080229.html">
           puts
it
          </a>
          , "There was no reason to suspect that a thirteen-year-old
honor-roll student with a clean disciplinary record had adopted
drug-smuggling practices associated with international
narcotrafficking, or to suppose that other middle-school students
would willingly consume ibuprofen that was stored in another
student's crotch."
         </p>
         <p>
          The invasiveness of the search also has to be weighed against
the evil it was aimed at preventing. "Remember," the school
district's lawyer recently
          <a href="http://www.abcnews.go.com/TheLaw/story?id=4537765&amp;page=1">
           told
          </a>
          ABC News by way of justification, "this was prescription-strength
ibuprofen." It's a good thing the school took swift action, before
anyone got unauthorized relief from menstrual cramps.
         </p>
         <p>
           Copyright 2008 by Creators Syndicate Inc.
         </p>
        </div>

            <a class="permalink" href="#comment_951317">
             #
            </a>
           </p>
           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             A side issue in this case is that it demonstrates what an
absolute hash the courts have made of search procedures because
they refuse to adopt the readily apparent hard and fast rules that
already exist in the Constitution.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             In order to facilitate, say, the searching of school lockers, all
that the courts had to do was declare that the school district is
the owner of all school property and that students are not leasees
of the locker space and have zero right to privacy or expectation
of privacy in that space. This would have given the schools the
authority to search lockers for truly dangerous items without
needing to obtain warrants, while protecting the
             <em>
              person
             </em>
             of
students from unreasonable and abusive searches like this
one.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             But because the property rights solution is too simple for our
asinine courts, they chose instead to craft special rules for
warrantless searches of school students, engaging in their usual
absurd pantomime of "balancing interests" that the Constitution
does not balance. So we end up with a case where poking a 13 year
old in the box may actually be permissible, depending on how this
court chooses to interpret extraordinarily vague and subjective
criteria like whether the search was "reasonably related in scope
to the circumstances which justified the interference in the first
place" or whether the search was "balanced" by the "interest" of
finding a prescription drug.
            </p>
           </div>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             <em>
              In order to facilitate, say, the searching of school
lockers, all that the courts had to do was declare that the school
district is the owner of all school property and that students are
not leasees of the locker space and have zero right to privacy or
expectation of privacy in that space. This would have given the
schools the authority to search lockers for truly dangerous items
without needing to obtain warrants, while protecting the person of
students from unreasonable and abusive searches like this
one.
             </em>
             <br/>
             <br/>
             The only problem with this is that many adult employees of schools
also have lockers, locked desk drawers, or similar storage places
that are entitled to a reasonable expectation of privacy. If
schools use a property-law exception to search school lockers, then
they have a right to search employee lockers. No employee would
stand for it.
            </p>
           </div>

right to do so and I can't stop them. The only things they cannot
search are my car and my person. However, if I don't consent to a
search of those I get fired. This has been the rule at every place
I've ever worked, and is usually explicitly spelled out in the
employee handbook.

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             I wish I could say I was surprised at this, but I can't.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             My young cousin (13) was told that he couldn't have contact lense
re-wetting solution in school. He had to get a written statement
from his optometrist saying that he may need to use it during the
course of the day, and it still couldn't be on his person-- like
all the other drugs, it had to remain behind lock and key in the
office. So whereas before he could administer the eyedrops in class
without disruption, now he has to ask the teacher to write him a
pass, walk down to the office, ask the secretary to get him an
administrator, and the administrator has to get the re-wetting
solution and give it to him.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             After all this, they
             <em>
              still
             </em>
             balked because the doctor's
note didn't specify a dosage or specific indications. Remember,
this is all for a buffered saline solution.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             In the same school, a family friend was issued a disciplinary
warning for having cough drops while she recovered from a cold.
Obviously, a strip search is a whole different level of personal
violation, but it seems like a natural progression from the way
things are around here.
            </p>
           </div>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             J sub D,
             <br/>
             <br/>
             I'm glad you challenged me because it made me look up the relevant
legal standard.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             "Applicability of the fourth amendment does not turn on the nature
of the property interest in the searched premises, but on the
reasonableness of the person's privacy expectation. . .
Furthermore, defendant's assertion that a public employer is free
to search the premises of an employee is a broad overstatement of
the relevant law. The cases indicate that an employer may conduct a
search in accordance with a regulation or practice that would
dispel in advance any expectations of privacy." Gillard v. Schmidt,
579 F.2d 825, 829 (3d Cir. 1978).
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Basically, if your school or other government employer has a policy
that areas to which you expect privacy will be routinely searched
for workplace reasons, then they can search those areas. That's why
Navy footlockers can get searched. However, the government can't
just go through your private stuff looking for contraband without
probable cause or some other exigent circumstance.
            </p>
           </div>

           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             As a member of that fourth (perhaps lower?)class of citizens
known as public school teachers that is reviled here with
near-religious fervor, I can offer no defense for this action or
this principal. The action taken is abhorrent to me personally, and
professionally, I would have stopped at the bookbag search and let
it go.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Neu Mejican, you commented that there was no new analysis being
offered. I wonder what else there is to do at this point except
bitch about the situation.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             As far as I know, no student has ever been strip-searched at my
school, but we have asked that they not bring glass bottles to
school (in the past they've broken them on the playground and
attacked each other) and to bring only unopened juice or soda on
class trips or with their lunches (in the past, they've filled them
with alcoholic beverages and caused lots of problems on class
trips).
             <br/>
             <br/>
             My school has more issues to contend with than the possibility of
smuggled Advil, but I do not believe my principal or any member of
the administration would ever suggest that we strip search a
student or go into lockers or bookbags without consent or
reasonable cause.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             I do understand that there are fine legal lines we have to tread
when it comes to student welfare and school safety. If we overstep
the bounds and accuse students of that which they are not guilty,
then the school is said to be heavy-handed. If we do not keep
illegal drugs or weapons out of the school, we are endangering the
whole student and staff population, and are guilty again.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             I attended private schools when I was young, and a public
high-school for three years. I saw little difference in the
policies between the two, and in fact I felt safer in my public
high school than I did in the private high school I attended my
Freshman year. I understand the benefits of school choice, but as
far as the benefits of a private education being better than
public, I have to wonder why it is a universally held belief that
one is inherently better, safer, and more reasonable in situations
where "zero tolerance" is being exercised.
            </p>
           </div>

           <div class="content">
            <p>
             Addendum to my post: the bookbag search would have been
conducted only if deemed absolutely necessary - quite a subjective
line of reasoning, I know, but I suppose it could be used as a
gesture to show activity on the part of the "responsible adults"
involved.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             I wonder how we expect kids to grow up into functional adults when
everything they do is minutely scrutinized and cast as wrong.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Literacy comes in all forms, including the ability to calculate
average gas mileage and understand a prescription bottle or OTC
medication instructions. Rather than having zero-T for all drugs,
why not teach kids the physiological effects of the medications,
how to read dosage instructions, and then trust them to exercise
that knowledge when it comes to self-medicating headaches and
sniffles?
            </p>

             #
            </a>
           </p>
           <!--Comment Body-->
           <div class="content">
            <p>
             First, this case demonstrates the absurdity of "zero tolerance"
-- which always seems to expand to cover irrelevant, harmless
items. Even granting the appropriateness of school rules against
recreational drugs, there is no justification for school rules
against medicines with no recreational potential.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Second, even if the student in question had the medicines, there
would be justification for the search. An appropriate response
would be to *educate* the student(s) regarding them. In particular,
it would be worth informing the student(s) that as ibuprofen and
naproxen are both NSAIDS, they should not be taken together.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Third: That said, I do not see why a *strip* search should make
this case such a big deal. Students have to strip completely and
walk around buck naked practically every day they go to school.
They do this when they take a shower in "physical education".
            </p>
           </div>

             <br/>
             <br/>
             Gather her belongings, and search her backpack, etc, and find
NOTHING.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             &gt;NOW&lt; authorities, get an inspiration, or according to the
judges a "reasonable expectation", that if they strip search her
and remove her bra and panties, that THEN they will find
contraband.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Pardon my French, but how the frick do they figure
that!??!?!?!
             <br/>
             <br/>
             So those judges are saying that if I accused them of selling drugs.
That the police would search their lockers, their offices and their
cars and houses.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             And find NOTHING.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             That the police would STILL have a "reasonable expectation" that if
they strip searched them and pulled their shorts off that they
would find drugs???
             <br/>
             <br/>
             HUH?? Maybe its just me, but I don't get it.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             If winning the "War on Drugs" depends on pulling the panties off of
women &amp; children, then we are in BIG trouble.
             <br/>
             <br/>
             The 4th amendment says "The right of the people to be secure in
their persons, houses, papers, and effects, against unreasonable
searches and seizures, shall not be violated, and no Warrants shall
issue, but upon probable cause, supported by Oath or affirmation,
and particularly describing the place to be searched, and the
persons or things to be seized."
             <br/>
             <br/>
             Now for the favor.please email the Attorney General of the United
States and see if we can get an answer from him.
             <br/>
             Dept of Justice United States : AskDOJ@usdoj.gov
            </p>
           </div>

      <script>
       $(document).ready(function() {
    	//no point in binding to swipe events if there's no touch support in the browser (and it goofs up selection)
		if ('ontouchstart' in window) {
			//in an effort to reduce false horizontal swipes from bold vertical flicks on larger screens...
			swipeThreshold = 200;
			$("#content-col").swipe( {
				threshold: swipeThreshold,
				allowPageScroll: 'vertical',
			    swipeLeft:function(event, direction, distance, duration, fingerCount) {
			    	//we're going to put in a non-zero fingercount check here to exclude mouse drags
					if (fingerCount &amp;&amp; $('#nextpage').length &amp;&amp; $('#nextpage').attr("href").length) {
					    window.location.href=  $('#nextpage').attr("href");
					}
			    },
			    swipeRight:function(event, direction, distance, duration, fingerCount) {
			    	//we're going to put in a non-zero fingercount check here to exclude mouse drags
					if (fingerCount &amp;&amp; $('#previouspage').length &amp;&amp; $('#previouspage').attr("href").length) {
				    	window.location.href = $('#previouspage').attr("href");
					}
			    }
			});
		}
    });
      </script>

        <script>
         $(function(){
	$("#topstoriessidebar .selector a").click(function(e){
		var $this=$(this), catref = $this.attr("data-category"),
			$sidebar = $this.parent().parent().parent();
		e.preventDefault();
		$sidebar.find('&gt; .selector &gt; li').removeClass('active');
		$this.parent().addClass('active');
		$sidebar.find('&gt; .inner &gt; .stories').hide().filter('[data-category='+catref+']').show();
	});
});
        </script>
